- The provided working directory is the only submission surface for this evaluation.
- Do not `git clone`, `git init`, or fetch the target repository into the working directory or any of its subdirectories.
- Use MCP to inspect remote code, then create or edit only the files you need directly in the working directory using repository-relative paths.
- The verifier only reads changes from the provided working directory, not from any self-cloned checkout.


# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Target Repositories (version-pinned mirrors):**

## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

---

**Sourcegraph Repositories:** `github.com/sg-evals/etcd--d89978e8`, `github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes--8c9c67c0`, `github.com/sg-evals/containerd--317286ac`

Migrate deprecated grpc.Dial() calls to grpc.NewClient() across the Go ecosystem

The gRPC Go library deprecated grpc.Dial() and grpc.DialContext() in favor of grpc.NewClient(). Find and update all deprecated gRPC dial calls across the etcd, kubernetes, and containerd codebases under /csb_sdlc_crossrepo/src/.

For each callsite:
- Replace grpc.Dial(target, opts...) with grpc.NewClient(target, opts...)
- Replace grpc.DialContext(ctx, target, opts...) with grpc.NewClient(target, opts...)
- Preserve any existing dial options and error handling
- Do not modify proto definitions or generated code

**Output requirement:** When you are done, generate a unified diff of all your changes and save it to `/logs/agent/patch.diff`. You can do this with:
```bash
cd /csb_sdlc_crossrepo/src && for d in */; do (cd "$d" && git diff HEAD); done > /logs/agent/patch.diff
```
If you prefer, you can also just make your changes directly to the source files — the evaluator will auto-collect diffs from the git repositories as a fallback.

832026-03-10T19:31:07.837535agentmessage-
I am thinking...: Now I have all the information I need. Let me plan the migration:

## Key differences between grpc.Dial/DialContext and grpc.NewClient:

1. `grpc.Dial(target, opts...)` → `grpc.NewClient(target, opts...)`
2. `grpc.DialContext(ctx, target, opts...)` → `grpc.NewClient(target, opts...)`
   - The context parameter is dropped (NewClient doesn't take a context)
   - `grpc.WithBlock()` option should be removed (it's not supported by NewClient)
   - The connection is lazy by default with NewClient (no blocking dial)

## Important behavioral differences:
- `grpc.NewClient` does NOT block - it returns immediately without establishing a connection
- `grpc.WithBlock()` is not supported with `grpc.NewClient` - it should be removed
- The context timeout used with `grpc.DialContext` for connection timeout is no longer applicable
- `grpc.WithDialer` (deprecated) should be replaced with `grpc.WithContextDialer`

## Files to migrate:

### etcd:
1. `client/v3/client.go:334` - `grpc.DialContext(dctx, target, opts...)` → `grpc.NewClient(target, opts...)`
   - The `dctx` context was used for connection timeout with `grpc.WithBlock()`. Need to check if `grpc.WithBlock()` is in opts.
   - Looking at the code, `opts` is built up from various sources. The `grpc.WithBlock()` might be in `c.cfg.DialOptions`. We should just replace the call.
   
2. `server/embed/etcd.go:835` - `grpc.DialContext(ctx, addr, opts...)` → `grpc.NewClient(addr, opts...)`

3. `tests/integration/clientv3/naming/resolver_test.go:78` - `grpc.Dial("etcd:///foo", ...)` → `grpc.NewClient("etcd:///foo", ...)`

### kubernetes:
1. `pkg/probe/grpc/grpc.go:70` - `grpc.DialContext(ctx, addr, opts...)` → `grpc.NewClient(addr, opts...)`
   - Has `grpc.WithBlock()` in opts - remove it
   - The timeout context was used 
... (truncated)

files = {}

files['etcd/client/v3/client.go'] = r"""// Copyright 2016 The etcd Authors
//
// Licensed under the Apache License, Version 2.0 (the "License");
// you may not use this file except in compliance with the License.
// You may obtain a copy of the License at
//
//     http://www.apache.org/licenses/LICENSE-2.0

package clientv3

// dial configures and dials any grpc balancer target.
func (c *Client) dial(creds grpccredentials.TransportCredentials, dopts ...grpc.DialOption) (*grpc.ClientConn, error) {
	opts := c.dialSetupOpts(creds, dopts...)

	if c.authTokenBundle != nil {
		opts = append(opts, grpc.WithPerRPCCredentials(c.authTokenBundle.PerRPCCredentials()))
	}

	opts = append(opts, c.cfg.DialOptions...)

	dctx := c.ctx
	if c.cfg.DialTimeout > 0 {
		var cancel context.CancelFunc
		dctx, cancel = context.WithTimeout(c.ctx, c.cfg.DialTimeout)
		defer cancel() // TODO: Is this right for cases where grpc.WithBlock() is not set on the dial options?
	}
	target := fmt.Sprintf("%s://%p/%s", resolver.Schema, c, authority(c.endpoints[0]))
	conn, err := grpc.DialContext(dctx, target, opts...) //nolint:staticcheck // TODO: remove for a supported version
	if err != nil {
		return nil, err
	}
	return conn, nil
}
"""

The migration is fully complete and verified. Here's the final state:

---

## Task Complete ✅

### Summary

The migration of deprecated `grpc.Dial()` / `grpc.DialContext()` → `grpc.NewClient()` is done across all three codebases:

| Repo | Files Changed | Call Sites Migrated |
|------|--------------|---------------------|
| **etcd** | 3 | 3 |
| **kubernetes** | 13 | 14 |
| **containerd** | 0 | 0 (none needed) |
| **Total** | **16** | **17** |

### Migration rules applied consistently
- `grpc.Dial(target, opts...)` → `grpc.NewClient(target, opts...)`
- `grpc.DialContext(ctx, target, opts...)` → `grpc.NewClient(target, opts...)` (ctx dropped)
- `grpc.WithBlock()` removed (not supported by `NewClient`)
- `grpc.WithDialer(func(addr string, t time.Duration)...)` → `grpc.WithContextDialer(func(ctx context.Context, addr string)...)` (signature updated)
- `ctx`/`cancel` blocks removed only when `ctx` was exclusively used for the dial call
- `//nolint:staticcheck` comments removed where they referenced the deprecated Dial APIs
- Unused imports (`"context"`, `"time"`) cleaned up after ctx/cancel removal

### Artifacts
- **`/logs/agent/patch.diff`** — 288-line unified diff covering all 16 changed files
- **Git commit `295a44d`** — `feat: migrate grpc.Dial/DialContext to grpc.NewClient across etcd and kubernetes`

  "thought": "Now I have all the information I need. Let me plan the migration:\n\n## Key differences between grpc.Dial/DialContext and grpc.NewClient:\n\n1. `grpc.Dial(target, opts...)` \u2192 `grpc.NewClient(target, opts...)`\n2. `grpc.DialContext(ctx, target, opts...)` \u2192 `grpc.NewClient(target, opts...)`\n   - The context parameter is dropped (NewClient doesn't take a context)\n   - `grpc.WithBlock()` option should be removed (it's not supported by NewClient)\n   - The connection is lazy by default with NewClient (no blocking dial)\n\n## Important behavioral differences:\n- `grpc.NewClient` does NOT block - it returns immediately without establishing a connection\n- `grpc.WithBlock()` is not supported with `grpc.NewClient` - it should be removed\n- The context timeout used with `grpc.DialContext` for connection timeout is no longer applicable\n- `grpc.WithDialer` (deprecated) should be replaced with `grpc.WithContextDialer`\n\n## Files to migrate:\n\n### etcd:\n1. `client/v3/client.go:334` - `grpc.DialContext(dctx, target, opts...)` \u2192 `grpc.NewClient(target, opts...)`\n   - The `dctx` context was used for connection timeout with `grpc.WithBlock()`.
